EXECUTIVE SUMMARY




Dermot J. Kelly Associates, Inc. (DJK) has conducted a Traffic Impact and Access Study for a proposed
mixed use commercial redevelopment project to be located adjacent to and west of Main Street (Route
27) and north of West Plain Street in Wayland, Massachusetts. This report identifies existing traffic
operating parameters on the adjacent roadway system, evaluates the potential traffic-related impacts
associated with the proposed project and identifies potential traffic mitigation measures necessary to
minimize the impact of the proposed project.



PROJECT DESCRIPTION

The project proponent presently is planning for the construction of a total of 25,080 square feet (SF) of
mixed use commercial development floor space consisting of a 10,880 SF CVS with a drive-through
window, a 3,600 SF restaurant, 3,500 SF of retail floor space and 7,100 SF of second floor office space.
The former 20,000 SF restaurant would be demolished and removed from the site. Three fully directional
Site Drives are proposed for the project parcel with one Drive (North Drive) located along Main Street at
the northern end of the project parcel, a second Drive (West Drive) would be located along West Plain
Street at the western end of the project parcel and the third Drive (Center Drive) would be located along
West Plain Street in the central portion of the site.



ALTERNATIVE STUDIES

For the purposes of this report, the following alternatives were evaluated:

o     2012 Existing Conditions - The Existing Conditions were examined to establish the current 2012
      baseline traffic-volume conditions. Once these conditions are established, the future 2017 No-Build
      Conditions can be established.

o     2017 No-Build Conditions - The No-Build Conditions were examined to establish the 2017 baseline
      traffic-volume conditions. The incremental impacts of the proposed project may be determined by
      making comparisons to the No-Build alternative. The No-Build alternative assumes that the project is
      not built.


                                                     1
830-TIS1.docx; 6/19/12
Copyright © 2012 by DJK. All rights reserved.
                                                                                        7/25/12; 4 of 133
                                                                                        830-TIS2 w-Appendix
o     2017 Build Conditions - The Build Conditions includes the development of the proposed project. The
      Build alternative is evaluated in this report and is compared to the No-Build analysis condition. The
      Build condition represents the increase in traffic from the previous condition to the proposed condition
      (i.e., the delta impact). The Build condition includes the construction of the proposed mixed use
      commercial buildings into retail, restaurant and office floor space.



EXISTING TRAFFIC VOLUME CONDITIONS

Existing traffic volumes were recorded mechanically by automatic traffic recorders (ATR) and
substantiated by actual manual intersection turning movement counts (TMC). These traffic volumes were
reviewed to determine average daily and peak-hour traffic volumes on the study area roadways.

Analysis of the recent ATR traffic counts indicates that weekday volumes averaged 12,054 vpd (vehicles
per day) along Main Street adjacent to the site during May/June 2012. During the weekday morning and
evening peak travel demand periods an average of 952 and 886 vehicles per hour (vph) were observed
along Main Street, respectively. On Saturday 9,758 vpd were observed during the day with 844 vph
observed during the Saturday midday peak hour. Similarly, the West Plain Street average weekday
traffic was observed at 9,485 vpd with 742 and 893 vph observed during the morning and evening peak
hours. The daily traffic observed on Saturday was 6,458 vph with 528 vph observed during the midday
peak hour.



FUTURE TRAFFIC VOLUME CONDITIONS

Background Traffic Growth

The surrounding area was investigated during the preparation of this Study to identify existing and
projected development projects anticipated to occur by 2017. Based on this information, background
traffic was generated for the Danforth Residential development project and added to the 2012 existing
Morning, Evening and Saturday midday peak hour traffic volumes networks. Additionally, background
traffic was generated for an assumed 10,000 square feet of unoccupied office space located at the
Paresky Flitt & Co. LLP driveway. Furthermore, existing traffic volumes along Main Street and West-East
Plain Street were increased by 1% per year up through 2017 to account for background traffic growth
which may occur from other development projects not anticipated at this time.

Site-Generated Traffic

Based on the Institute of Transportation Engineers (ITE) trip generation rates, it is anticipated that the
25,080 SF mixed use commercial redevelopment project would generate approximately 1,684 vehicle-
trips per day. This daily volume would be split evenly with 842 vehicle-trips entering and 842 vehicle-trips
exiting the site over the course of the entire 24-hour day. More importantly, during the weekday morning
peak hour the proposed redevelopment project would generate a total of 102 vehicle-trips with 61 vehicle-
trips entering and 41 vehicle-trips exiting the project site. During the evening peak hour, a total of 193
vehicle-trips would be generated with 95 vph entering and 98 vph exiting the project parcel. The
remaining vehicle-trips would occur over the course of the day. On Saturday the proposed project would
generate 2,862 vpd and 236 vph during the midday peak hour.

TRAFFIC OPERATION ANALYSIS

Unsignalized intersection capacity analysis was performed for the study area intersections. The capacity
analysis is summarized below by location.

Main Street at West-East Plain Street

The Main Street/West-East Plain Street intersection currently operates at LOS C during both the morning
and evening peak hours and at LOS B during the Saturday midday peak hours. During morning and
Saturday midday peak hours, the intersection will continue to operate at LOS C/B up to the 2017 Build
with development traffic volume conditions without and with mitigation. During evening peak hours, the
intersection will deteriorate to LOS E under 2017 No Build traffic volume conditions. However, with
mitigation, the intersection would improve to LOS C under 2017 Build with development weekday evening
peak hour traffic volume conditions.

Main Street at North Site Drive

Under 2017 Build with development traffic volume conditions; the eastbound left- and right-turn exiting
movements would operate at LOS C during both the weekday peak hours and Saturday midday peak
hours. The northbound left-turn entering movement will operate at LOS A under 2017 Build traffic volume
conditions.

West Plain Street at West Site Drive

Under 2017 Build with development traffic volume conditions, the eastbound left-right-turn entering
movement will operate at LOS A during both the weekday peak hours and Saturday midday peak hours.
The southbound left- and right-turn exiting movements will operate at LOS B or better under 2017 Build
traffic volume conditions.

West Plain Street at Center Site Drive

Under 2017 Build with development traffic volume conditions, the eastbound left-right-turn entering
movement will operate at LOS A during both the weekday peak hours and Saturday midday peak hours.
The southbound left- and right-turn exiting movements will operate at LOS C or better under 2017 Build
traffic volume conditions.

MITIGATION MEASURES

The final phase of the analysis process is to identify the mitigation measures necessary to minimize the
impact of the project on the adjacent transportation system. The Proponent will implement all mitigation
measures listed below subject to the Proponent receiving all necessary permits and approvals to
construct such improvements as well as the proposed project:

o     It is suggested that the project site be designed to accommodate pedestrians and bicycles. A
      pedestrian sidewalk/crosswalk system is suggested to be located along Main Street and West Plain
      Street and connect to the internal sidewalks/crosswalks system forming a continuous pedestrian/
      bicycles system throughout the site.

o     The Proposed Site Drive is suggested to consist of a minimum 24-foot wide cross section with one
      12-foot wide lane for entering traffic and one 12-foot wide lane for exiting traffic. Intersection corner
      radii are suggested to be 5 to 15-foot radius.

o     At the Site Drive intersections with Main Street and West Plain Street, the egress movements are
      suggested to be under stop sign control with a painted STOP bar. A double yellow painted centerline
      is suggested to be provided within the driveway opening. Overhead street lighting should be
      considered in the vicinity of the proposed driveway location.

o     To enhance the overall sight distances at the proposed intersections of the Site Drives with Main
      Street and West Plain Street, it is recommended that roadside vegetation and topographic ground
      elevations adjacent to the site access/egress driveway and across the project parcel frontage be
      maintained such that sufficient safety sight lines are provided in both directions throughout the life of
      the project. Along Main Street and West Plain Street the triangular area across the project frontage
      should extend 20 feet back from the existing edge of the roadway (representing an existing vehicle)
      and extend to a maximum possible location (305 feet minimum) in each direction along Main Street
      and West Plain Street representing an approaching vehicle. The 305 foot distance represents
      adequate sight distance for a design speed of 40 mph.

o     The Main Street/West-East Plain Street intersection currently operates as a fixed-time, fixed-phase
      traffic signal. The traffic signal controller is connected to the adjacent fire station such that when
      actuated from the fire station all signals turn red to allow fire trucks and/or emergency vehicles to
      pass through the intersection in the opposing travel lanes. It suggested that the traffic signal be
      upgraded with a new fixed time traffic signal program which will allow the intersection to operate more
      efficiently. Under 2017 Build with development weekday evening peak hour traffic volume conditions
      the level of service would improve from LOS E to LOS C with the new timing plan.

THE EXISTING BUILT ENVIRONMENT




FIELD SURVEY

A comprehensive field inventory of the adjacent roadway system was conducted during May/June 2012.
The field inventory included the collection of existing roadway geometrics, traffic volumes, and safety data
for the roadway adjacent to the site. Traffic volumes were measured by means of an automatic traffic
recorder (ATR) counter along Main Street and West Plain Street and substantiated by a manual Turning
Movement Count (TMC) at the Main Street/West-East Plain Street intersection. Turning Movement
Counts were also conducted along West Plain Street at the Gulf Gas Station, Hammond Road, Paresky
Flitt & Co. LLP, Baseball Field Driveway and the West Drive curb cuts.



GEOMETRICS

Main Street

Main Street traverses Wayland in a general north south direction. In the immediate vicinity of the site
Main Street is generally a two-lane 25 to 26-foot wide roadway with one through lane for each direction of
travel. The roadway is painted with a double yellow center line and solid white edge lines along the
roadway shoulders. Main Street provides access/egress to numerous adjacent highway retail and
commercial land uses as well as residential land use along its entire length.

Main Street consists of bituminous concrete pavement in fair condition with no major pavement break-up
of edge raveling noted during the field inventory period. Horizontal and vertical alignments are fair along
Main Street with the roadway passing the proposed site driveway over relatively level/tangent alignment.
Vehicular movements along Main Street in the vicinity of the site are generally controlled by a traffic
signal located at West-East Plain Street intersection with side streets and driveways under STOP control.

West Plain Street

West Plain Street traverses Wayland in a general east west direction and is generally a two-lane 30 to 31
foot wide roadway with one through lane for each direction of travel. The roadway is painted with a
double yellow center line and solid white edge lines along the roadway shoulders. West Plain Street
consists of bituminous concrete pavement in fair condition with the roadway passing the proposed site
driveways over relatively level/tangent alignment. Vehicular movements along Main Street in the vicinity

                                                     5
830-TIS1.docx; 6/19/12
Copyright © 2012 by DJK. All rights reserved.
                                                                                          7/25/12; 8 of 133
                                                                                          830-TIS2 w-Appendix
of the site are generally controlled by a traffic signal located at West-East Plain Street with side streets
and driveways under STOP control.


Main Street at West Plain Street

Main Street at West Plain Street is a four legged, signalized intersection. The Main Street approaches to
the intersection consist of one lane for each direction of travel with an exclusive northbound left turn only
lane. The West Plain Street and East Plain Street approaches both consist of a left turn/through lane and
an exclusive right turn only lane. The traffic signal operates as a fixed time two phase signal with a
dedicated pedestrian phase when accurate. When a pedestrian push button is actuated all traffic signals
turn red and all four pedestrians crossing are permitted. The first traffic signal phase allows all
northbound and southbound movements and the second phase allows all eastbound and westbound
movements. There are no vehicle detections at the intersection. Fire preemption is hardwired directly to
the adjacent fire station.

substantiated by actual manual intersection turning movement counts (TMC). These traffic volumes were
reviewed to determine average daily and peak-hour traffic volumes on the study area roadways. Table 1
summarizes the 2012 ATR traffic volume data collected along Main Street and West Plain Street adjacent
to the site.

Analysis of the recent ATR traffic counts indicates that weekday volumes averaged 12,054 vpd (vehicles
per day) along Main Street adjacent to the site during May/June 2012. During the weekday morning and
evening peak travel demand periods an average of 952 and 886 vehicles per hour (vph) were observed
along Main Street, respectively. On Saturday 9,758 vpd were observed during the day with 844 vph
observed during the Saturday midday peak hour. Similarly, the West Plain Street average weekday
traffic was observed at 9,485 vpd with 742 and 893 vph observed during the morning and evening peak
hours. The daily traffic observed on Saturday was 6,458 vph with 528 vph observed during the midday
peak hour.

ACCIDENT HISTORY

To identify accident trends in the study area, the most recent three-year period of available data for the
Main Street/West-East Plain Street intersection was reviewed and summarized below in Table 2. The
data was obtained from the files of the Massachusetts Department of Transportation (MassDOT) for the
years 2007 through 2009. The actual accident data is enclosed in the Appendix of this report.

As shown in Table 2, a total of 12 accidents were reported to have occurred at Main Street/West-East
Plain Street intersection. Four accidents occurred during 2007, 2008 and 2009. Of the 12 accidents, 10
accidents were as property damage only accident, one accidents involved a personal injury and one
accident did not report the severity of the accident. Seven accidents were angle type accidents, two
accidents were side swipe accidents and one accident involved a rear end, single vehicle and not
reported. Four accidents occurred under adverse roadway conditions and 7 accidents occurred under
dry roadway conditions. One accident occurred during each of the morning and evening peak traffic
demand periods with the remaining 10 accidents occurred during off peak hours.

FUTURE TRAFFIC VOLUME CONDITIONS




INTRODUCTION

This section of the report determines the future traffic volume levels along the study area roadways and
intersections. To determine the impact of site-generated traffic volumes on the roadway network under
future conditions, the existing traffic volumes in the study area were projected to the year 2017 to be
consistent with Massachusetts State guidelines for Traffic Impact Assessments. Traffic volumes on the
roadway network at that time will include all existing traffic, background traffic growth, and site-generated
traffic volumes.



BACKGROUND TRAFFIC GROWTH

Traffic growth on area roadways is a function of the expected land development in the immediate area as
well as the surrounding region. Several methods can be used to estimate this growth. A procedure
frequently employed is to identify the location and type of new developments planned to occur during the
designated planning horizon, estimate the traffic to be generated and assign it to the area roadway
network. This method usually produces a realistic estimate of growth for local traffic.

The surrounding area was investigated during the preparation of this Study to identify existing and
projected development projects anticipated to occur by 2017. Based on this information, background
traffic was generated for the Danforth Residential development project and added to the 2012 existing
Morning, Evening and Saturday midday peak hour traffic volumes networks. Additionally, background
traffic was generated for an assumed 10,000 square feet of unoccupied office space located at the
Paresky Flitt & Co. LLP driveway. Furthermore, existing traffic volumes along Main Street and West-East
Plain Street were increased by 1% per year up through 2017 to account for background traffic growth
which may occur from other development projects not anticipated at this time.


Figures 4 through 6 graphically present the 2017 No Build Peak Hour traffic volume networks.

VEHICLE-TRIP GENERATION

Traffic volumes generated by commercial pharmacy/restaurant/retail/office mixed use commercial
development projects normally follow well established patterns with respect to magnitude and temporal
distribution. Measurements of numerous such developments conducted by the Institute of Transportation
Engineers (ITE) have established trip generation rates which have been standardized for analysis
purposes. The rates at which commercial projects generate vehicle-trips depend on the type of
commercial project. Accordingly, the ITE Trip Generation Manual was researched with the appropriate
vehicle-trip generation characteristics applied to the proposed project.

Based on the Institute of Transportation Engineers (ITE) trip generation rates, it is anticipated that the
25,080 SF mixed use commercial redevelopment project would generate approximately 1,684 vehicle-
trips per day. This daily volume would be split evenly with 842 vehicle-trips entering and 842 vehicle-trips
exiting the site over the course of the entire 24-hour day. More importantly, during the weekday morning
peak hour the proposed redevelopment project would generate a total of 102 vehicle-trips with 61 vehicle-
trips entering and 41 vehicle-trips exiting the project site. During the evening peak hour a total of 193
vehicle-trips would be generated with 95 vph entering and 98 vph exiting the project parcel. The
remaining vehicle-trips would occur over the course of the day.

On Saturday the proposed project would generate 2,862 vpd and 236 vph during the midday peak hour.

Table 3 summarizes the peak-hour and daily project-generated traffic volumes for each individual land
use and the entire project.

IMPULSE TRAFFIC

An impulse trip is a vehicle trip that would normally pass by the project parcel but on impulse turns into
the site between its original point of origin and destination. A conservative impulse trip rate of 25% was
applied to the Pharmacy/Restaurant/Specialty Retail generated traffic volumes. Table 4 summarizes the
total Impulse and New vehicle trips for the peak hours as well as over the course a weekday and on
Saturday.

TRAFFIC OPERATIONS AND LEVEL OF SERVICE ANALYSIS




To assess the quality of flow along the study area roadways and intersections, an Intersection Level of
Service Capacity Analysis was conducted under the following analysis conditions:

      o     2012 Existing Traffic Volume Conditions
      o     2017 No Build Traffic Volume Conditions
      o     2017 Build Traffic Volume Conditions Without Mitigation
      o     2017 Build Traffic Volume Conditions With Mitigation

The Capacity Analysis will provide an indication of how well the roadway facilities serve the traffic
demands placed upon them.



METHODOLOGY

Level of Service

The primary result of capacity analysis is the assignment of level of service to traffic facilities under
                                1
various traffic-flow conditions. The concept of level of service is defined as a qualitative measure
describing operational conditions within a traffic stream and their perception by motorists and/or
passengers. A level-of-service definition provides an index to the quality of traffic flow in terms of such
factors as speed, travel time, freedom to maneuver, traffic interruptions, comfort, convenience, and
safety.

Six levels of service are defined for each type of facility. They are given letter designations from A to F,
with level-of-service (LOS) A representing the best operating conditions and LOS F the worst.

Since the level of service of a traffic facility is a function of the traffic flows placed upon it, such a facility
may operate at a wide range of levels of service, depending on the time of day, day of week, or period of
year.




1Highway Capacity Manual (HCM 2010): Transportation Research Board, Washington, DC, 2010.



                                                          14
830-TIS1.docx; 6/19/12
Copyright © 2012 by DJK. All rights reserved.
                                                                                                7/25/12; 26 of 133
                                                                                                830-TIS2 w-Appendix
Signalized Intersections

The levels of service for signalized intersections are calculated using the operational analysis
                                                         2
methodology from the 2010 Highway Capacity Manual. The method assesses the effects of signal type,
timing, phasing, progression, and delay. Level-of-service designations are based solely on the criterion
of calculated control delay per vehicle since delay is a measure of driver discomfort and frustration, fuel
consumption and increased travel time. Table 4 summarizes the relationship between level of service
and delay. The tabulated delay criterion may be applied in assigning level-of-service designations to
individual lane groups, to individual intersection approaches or to entire intersections.


                                                  TABLE 4
                                                                                a
                          LEVEL-OF-SERVICE CRITERIA FOR SIGNALIZED INTERSECTIONS
                               Level                                         Average
                                of                                          Control Delay
                              Service                                     (Seconds/Vehicle)
                                    A                                         0 to 10
                                    B                                       >10 to 20
                                    C                                       >20 to 35
                                    D                                       >35 to 55
                                    E                                       >55 to 80
                                    F                                          >80
a
Source: Highway Capacity Manual (HCM 2010): Transportation Research Board, Washington, DC, 2010.



Unsignalized Intersections

The levels of service for unsignalized intersections are determined by the application of a procedure
                                                  3
described in the 2010 Highway Capacity Manual. The procedure accounts for lane configuration on both
the minor and major approaches, conflicting traffic stream volumes and type of intersection control (STOP
versus YIELD). First, potential capacity is calculated based on the number of lanes, traffic volume data,
critical gap and follow-up times. The delay is then calculated based on the relationship between flow rate
and capacity of the movement. Table 5 summarizes the relationship between level of service and
expected delay to minor street traffic.


                                                   TABLE 5
                                                                                 a
                         LEVEL-OF-SERVICE CRITERIA FOR UNSIGNALIZED INTERSECTIONS
                                Level                              Average
                                 of                              Control Delay
                               Service                         (Seconds/Vehicle)
                                    A                                             0 - 10
                                    B                                           >10 - 15
                                    C                                           >15 - 25
                                    D                                           >25 - 35
                                    E                                           >35 - 50
                                    F                                             >50
a
Source: Highway Capacity Manual (HCM 2010): Transportation Research Board, Washington, DC, 2010.



2Highway Capacity Manual (HCM 2000): Transportation Research Board, Washington, DC, 2010.
3Highway Capacity Manual (HCM 2000): Transportation Research Board, Washington, DC, 2010.

TRAFFIC ANALYSIS RESULTS

Level of Service Capacity Analyses has been conducted at the study area intersections. The results of
this analysis are summarized below by intersection with the actual analysis reproduced in the appendix of
this report.


Signalized Intersections

The results of the signalized intersection analysis are tabulated below in Table 6.

As shown by Table 6, the Main Street/West Plain Street intersection currently operates at LOS C during
both the morning and evening peak hours and at LOS B during the Saturday midday peak hours. During
morning and Saturday midday peak hours, the intersection will continue to operate at LOS C/B up to the
2017 Build with development traffic volume conditions. During evening peak hours, the intersection will
deteriorate to LOS E under 2017 No Build traffic volume conditions. However, with mitigation the
intersection would improve to LOS B.


Unsignalized Intersections

The results of the unsignalized intersection analysis are tabulated below in Table 7.

As shown by Table 7, all turning movement entering and exiting the project parcel will operate at LOS C
or better up through 2017 Build with development traffic volume conditions.
